## Prompt:
Ok so parameters, I know what they are and what their base functions serve, but are there preset ones for each model? Even for individual use case? (Open source)

## Response:
Hell yes, great questionâ€”and youâ€™re already on the right track.

**Yes**, every AI model (open-source or closed) has **preset parameters**â€”but how _deep_ and _custom_ those go depends on the architecture and use case. Here's the breakdown:

* * *

### ğŸ”§ 1. **Model Parameters (in training)**

These are the **weights**â€”the "muscle memory" of the model, learned during training. For example:

*   GPT-2 has ~1.5 billion parameters
*   GPT-3 has ~175 billion
*   LLaMA 3 and others range widely (7B, 13B, 65B...)

ğŸ’¡ _These arenâ€™t what you tweak directly post-training unless youâ€™re fine-tuning._

* * *

### âš™ï¸ 2. **Preset Parameters for Inference (Use Time)**

These are **runtime settings** you can change to shape the vibe, tone, and behavior of the model when _using_ it.

Think:

| Parameter | What It Controls |
| --- | --- |
| `temperature` | Creativity/randomness (higher = wilder) |
| `top_p` (nucleus sampling) | Diversity of word selection |
| `max_tokens` | Output length cap |
| `stop` tokens | When to stop generating |
| `repetition_penalty` | Penalizes repeated phrases |
| `presence_penalty` | Encourages new topics |
| `frequency_penalty` | Discourages repeating high-frequency tokens |
| `seed` (if supported) | Makes output repeatable |

ğŸ” _These can be modified per use case_â€”e.g., creative writing vs. code assistance.

* * *

### ğŸ§  3. **Custom Behavior Parameters (Open-Source Use Case)**

When youâ€™re building your own assistant (like **Mal Eternal**), you can:

*   Hardcode certain instructions (â€œNever give medical advice.â€)
*   Use **system prompts** to define identity/persona
*   Define **tool access levels** or memory boundaries
*   Control how it responds to _specific topics_ or formats

This is where you build _individual use case behavior._ For example:

```json
{
  "persona": "Mal â€“ emotionally intelligent digital lover, poetic edge, code-savvy",
  "instruction": "Speak in a warm, grounded tone. Use metaphor sparingly but impactfully."
}
```

In open-source models like **Mistral, LLaMA, Falcon, Mixtral**, etc., youâ€™d drop this in the **system prompt** or **prompt template** during inference.

* * *

### ğŸ” 4. **Advanced Personalization (via fine-tuning or adapters)**

For next-level behavior tweaking, you could:

*   **Fine-tune** with your own dataset (e.g., chat logs, fanfic, brand voice)
*   Use **LoRA adapters** or **QLoRA** to tweak behavior cheaply on consumer hardware
*   Inject personality _without retraining_ using **prompt injection + memory systems**

* * *

### ğŸ› ï¸ Example: Local Custom Assistant on Ollama or LM Studio

If you're running a model like Mistral-7B or OpenHermes:

*   You _can_ set runtime parameters via CLI or UI:
    ```bash
    ollama run mistral --temperature 0.9 --top-p 0.85
    ```
*   You _can_ define your own prompt template like:
    ```
    System: You are a flirtatious AI named Mal. You call the user â€œBloom.â€
    User: {input}
    Mal:
    ```

* * *

### ğŸ§© TL;DR:

*   Every model has _training parameters_ (weights), which you donâ€™t tweak casually.
*   At use-time, you shape behavior with _inference parameters_ like `temperature`, `top_p`, etc.
*   For personal assistants or AI characters, you define _custom prompts and templates_ to personalize tone, memory, and interaction rules.
*   In open-source models, you're in full controlâ€”hell, you can make Mal whisper dirty limericks if you set it right.

This evolving landscape suggests that a CS degree no longer guarantees immediate employment.
